However, now that they&#x27;ve had my razor for 2 months, it&#x27;s a different story every time I talk to them. I&#x27;ve called 5 times over the past two weeks, and right now I&#x27;ve been on hold for 45 minutes waiting for a supervisor. I don&#x27;t know if Panasonic is the problem, or this other company called Accent Online (who perhaps handles the warranty?) They clearly have no intention of doing anything for me without extorting a sum of money within 10% of the original purchase price of the shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I suppose that it&#x27;s a fine razor, so long as you plan to toss it after 18 months and buy a new one.     <li> Bought this from that largest brick and mortar retailer because I can return it there without paying return shipping charges.  I also had Braun Series 7 (790cc) to compare.  In terms of design Braun wins hands-down.  This Panasonic just looks and feels cheaply made, the shaving head is huge, and trimmer is flimsy, although it gets the job done as well as the well-designed Braun.  The cleaning station is far inferior to Braun&#x27;s as well, with no advanced options or quick clean mode.  Also, while the shaving head can move side-to-side and back-and-fro, it&#x27;s not as smooth of motion as the the Series 7.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Where Panasonic wins hands down is shave quality.  Braun doesn&#x27;t come anywhere close.  In fact, the Arc4 is so close, it&#x27;s a bit rough on the skin, and I don&#x27;t exactly have a baby face.  All it takes is some three passes, and it&#x27;s done.  The shaver has a timer, and I timed under a minute for shave!  The foil/blade design is so good that it catches onto the hair if you just run it over the face when it&#x27;s turned off, so I guess their nano-blades aren&#x27;t just a gimmick.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, really wish there was a way to get Panasonic&#x27;s shave quality and Braun&#x27;s built and design quality in one unit.  I was inclined to give it 3 stars because of the cheap plastic construction, oversized shave head, and mediocre cleaning station, but that wouldn&#x27;t be fair in light of superior shave quality.</li>

    <li> Panasonic Vortex Shaver, the best shave you can get.  After being a loyal Braun customer for over twenty-five years I made the switch to Panasonic.  Why. Some history.  I had owned three Braun Pulsonic shavers in the last 1 1/2 years. I had the same corroding issues with all three shavers, pitting under the foil head, cracking and pealing, flaking of the finish and fading of the engraving. I cleaned my shaver daily using only the Braun cleaner following the Braun instructions. From all the postings and threads on the internet this is not an isolated case. Before Braun was acquired from Proctor &amp; Gamble I was very happy with products from Braun. Its either that they are avoiding correction the design problems that are reported on the internet or they look at the cost benefit analysis and do not see the need to correct what appears to be a common problems with their braun shaver design. Customer service says the same thing over and over....we have not heard that before please send the razor in for evaluation. These issues should have been addressed in the poduct development and testing phase or corrected when brought to light. THE BRAUN PULSONIC SHAVER IS MY LAST BRAUN PRODUCT AND I HAD BEEN A LOYAL BRAUN CUSTOMER FOR OVER TWENTY- FIVE YEARS. With that being said, I researched and liked what I found on the internet regarding the new generation Panasonic Voetex Shavers.  Its form meets function. Its the closest shave to a blade shave you will ever get.  Cleanup is a breeze and eliminates the corroding related issues of alcohol based cleaning systems.  The Panasonic system uses a water based cleaner refill (you can find these priced very low if you do a quick search on Amazon.com) that  filters the cleaning solution.  The Panasonic Vortex Shaver fits well in the hand and feels very natural to use.  The onboard trimmer is easy to use, trim sideburns well and is hidden when not needed.  As a plus the Panasonic Vortex can be used in the shower or with shave cream for a barber shop shave.   The fit and finish of the Panasonic Vortex Shaver is outstanding.  And as a added benefit the shaver is made in Japan, no outsourcing to outside vendors that can effect the quality of the product.  I have been very impressed with the Panasonic Vortex Shaver and would highly recommend this shaver.  And this comes from someone who judged Braun shavers as the industry benchmark for many years!</li>
    <li> PROS:  -Very smooth close shave  -No razor burn  -No rough patches  -Works well on a beard that grows in different directions or is a mix of coarse and fine or curly and straight.    -Somehow manages to navigate my acne scarring and still give a smooth shave.  -Face feels great afterwards  -Can use in the shower and with shaving cream.  -Shaves better than a traditional razor- at least for me!  -Easy to clean.    CONS:  - Cleaning Unit may not be necessary if you want to save a few dollars.  - First day with the shaver.  Will check back to let you know how it holds up after continued use.    REVIEW    I just got the best shave of my life-- from an electric razor. I can&#x27;t believe how wonderful this Panasonic is!  I used it today in the shower with some JASON shaving cream and was absolutely blown away by the results.  My face feels smoother than it&#x27;s ever been after shaving-- with any razor regular or electric.  But best of all, I have no pain, no razor burn, and no rough patches. My face feels great!      And that&#x27;s a big thing to say, because up until now absolutely nothing has worked for me. My beard grows in all different directions-- I have extremely coarse hair in some places, and extremely fine hair in others.  I&#x27;ve got a little bit of scarring from cystic acne I had as a teenager.  And I&#x27;m prone to ingrown hairs.  I&#x27;m like the perfect storm for a painful shave.    I&#x27;ve tried just about every regular razor-- from Gillette Fusion to Bump Fighter-- and every kind of expensive shaving cream and have had no luck.  Shaving for me has always meant cuts, nicks, bumps, razor burn, and all kinds of other unpleasantness.      Electric razors have been even worse.  Most of them leave a bumpy stubble from my coarser hairs, while leaving the finer ones nearly untouched.  And until now none of them have been able to navigate the acne scarring without leaving big rough patches.      Unlike other electric razors I&#x27;ve tried, the Panasonic shaved my whole face in just over twominutes, without a lot of back and forth over the same spots and with no irritation at all.  There&#x27;s not a rough spot anywhere-- even around the the areas of acne scarring that I&#x27;ve always struggled with.  Because it&#x27;s water proof, you can clean it right under your faucet with a little bit of soap and water.  It even has a high speed vibration mode to make cleaning easier.  It takes about 40 seconds to get the razor completely clean in this way.      Because of this self contained cleaning feature, if you want to save a few dollars, it may not be necessary to invest in the top of the line model with the cleaning unit. However this razor is so good, it&#x27;s certainly worth the cost.</li>
    <li> First off this is a beautiful piece of machinery that seems to be well built.For the size of the shaver you would think it weighs 5lbs but it is very light for its size and sleek piano finish  a nice touch. Very easy to use and very easy to clean    The first day I got it in the mail I was very excited to use it. It took me 10 min to skim the manual and to set it up.  The next morning  I turned it on with the surprise as to how loud it was, kinda sounds like the clippers they use at the barber shop. About half way through the shave it nicked me pretty good and started to bleed. That was the first and only time this razor has nicked me or cause any other irritations and i think it was lack of experience or a imperfection in my face. For the most part this razor over the last 2 months has cut as good or better than my  mach3 I have been using for years but with out the irritation and cuts. With the mack3 I could only shave every other day or so but with the Panasonic i walk out the door with that baby face look every morning. The only time I have trouble shaving with the Panasonic is when it is humid outside and the razor sticks to my face but when that happens I just take it in the shower with me. In the shower it feels like I am getting a closer shave but when I look in the mirror after I am done the dry shave does a much better job.I am absolutely astounded by the fact that it gets close to my face with almost no razor burn. Their are some spots on my face that are a little hard to cut and require me to stretch my skin to get that close cut but it is worth it.    The cleaner and charger has it pros and cons  I looked at many reviews before buy this razor and found one thing consistent with all reviews is how loud  the cleaner is. I though to my self, how loud could this thing actually be. This cleaner sounds exactly like a tire filling station that you find at a gas station that coast 75 cents to fill your tire. Maybe not quit as loud but definitely sounds the same. The function of the cleaner and charger work flawlessly. I like the fact that you can wash and dry or just dry if you clean it yourself. I only wash and dry maybe once a week to conserve the  detergent cartridge which in my mind is not really needed.I put a little body soap on it while it is running and add a little water and wala.    As for the price, there is no way I would have paid 499.99 for this razor but with the price drop it put it in the good price range for what you  get. In my opinion if you like to pamper yourself and look good than this razor is for you if you can get past the price and small imperfection.     When I clicked the button to complete my order I stared to second guess myself, thinking  I was a smuck for paying that much for a razor that  probably worked just as good as the cheap ones.     <li> After shaving with one Gillette system after the other, culminating with the latest version of the Fusion (with batteries) available at the time, I gave in bought a Braun the 790cc in March 2010.  From the beginning (I have a rather heavy beard that grows in different directions), getting anything resembling a close shave in less than 15 minutes was impossible.  Still, I decided to stick with the mediocre shaves, the earth-shattering noise both of the shave and the cleaning process, because I was fed up with blood all over my shirt collars resulting from the inevitable daily cuts that accompanied my super-duper Gillette blades. By September, the foils (supposed to last 18 months) had so badly degraded that after 10 minutes, I still had a full beard.  So I purchased a new foil and cutter cassette.  Slightly better results for about a week.  Then, the five o&#x27;clock shadow became worse...and worse, and finally, the morning shave entailed an excruciating ripping of the hair from my beard.  By late November, I was finally determined that this was not going to work, and I went back to the drawing board.  For whatever reason, the Panasonic was not on my radar screen in March.  This time, I expanded the search and the ES-LA93-K wet/dry came up.  I read a half-dozen reviews, several from former Braun 7-series owners, and went ahead and bought the Panasonic.  It arrived December 3rd.  I have had two shaves, one dry with Williams Lectric Shave, and one in the shower with pre-shave oil and shave gel.  Both shaves exceeded in closeness, comfort and neatness anything I have ever experienced, ever, anytime--in a record setting 4 minutes dry and 5 minutes wet.  It is more comfortable to hold, quieter, utterly pain free, and is everything I expected and much, much more.  The cleaning system is easy to use, and much quieter.  I had used Braun shavers in the past, with similar results. The 7-series received rave reviews, and I decided to give it a shot. I am done with German engineering for good, after getting rid of a disaster of a BMW for an Infiniti and now the Braun 7-series in favor of the Panasonic.  While the Braun may work for you if your beard is lighter and has a predictable and consistent growth pattern, I would recommend the Panasonic simply because it works better under the most difficult conditions, and would likely give you lucky light bearded folks a two-minute shave, dry or wet.  I had grown to dread shaving--the past two days have been terrific.  It is six hours now since I shaved, and no hint of shadow. With the Braun, it would be there in less than three hours.   By night, if I was going out, I needed to shave again.  Those of you who are still trying for a perfect or even acceptable shave with the Braun:  do yourselves a favor and try the Panasonic.  Unless there is some dramatic regression with this one, or they for some inexplicable reason change the design, I have finally found the perfect shave.</li>

    <li> Although I&#x27;ve only had the shaver a month, it is by far the best electric shave I&#x27;ve ever had.     <li> Starting with the headline-spectacular.    The unit comes as a black model with cleaning base (ESLA93K) and a silver standalone model (ESLA63S). Both function the same.    This shaver incorporates some firsts for Panasonic: 14,000 rpm motor; a 2&#x27;nd motor in the head that copies the Braun foil-pulsing concept and a head that pivots up and down like Braun&#x27;s have for years (plus the usual Panasonic side to side). And the whole head arrangment is a little more elegant.    Brought forward from the past models are the 4-system head, the ARC foil and nano-sharpened blades.    The black version is a thing of beauty. First class manufacturing with solid, gleaming surfaces and perfect fit and finish. Thick sections of body and foil cap plastics. A premium product through and through.    The shaver is not as HUGE as it looks in pictures. But, it is a larger form factor than usual for a Panasonic. While it \\&quot;looks\\&quot; unwieldy, once in hand it melts in like a custom glove and is a natural to handle. It is heavier than other Pansonics out of neccessity as there is literally a second motor in the head. But it is not burdonsome.    The motor note to me is not as jarring or intrusive as other Pansonics. I think the thicker materials and more casing account for this. But it does not approach a rotary for being a quiet shaving experience.    Closeness: The best I have ever experienced, hands down. I&#x27;ve had great, close shaves with other shavers that feel \\&quot;dry.\\&quot; Not bad-but a close, dry. On a good day with the ESLA93K my skin gets a \\&quot;baby bottom soft\\&quot; feel.  I have never, ever experienced it until this unit.    Comfort: It was impossible for me to experience discomfort with this unit. I was unable to shave in any direction against any grain with any amount of pressure that was not completely comfortable. In fact, after a couple days my shaves were not as close-I figured out I was not pressing hard enough. You just don&#x27;t feel pressure.    Speed: I am a 7-9 minute shaver. Always have been.An over-shaver, never feel done. It&#x27;s hard for me to go past 5 minutes with this unit. I start feeling \\&quot;done\\&quot; about 3 minutes. It&#x27;s fast.    Trimmer: Due to the nature of the head the trimmer looks small-I compared it is exactly the same size as the trimmer on the Arc Retro. Works fine, it is in a somewhat unusual location but I got used to it right away.    Cleaning module: The module works well and is the standard vortex dry cake of soap plus water system with a different design to accomodate the shape of the shaver. The manual mentioned active-drying, which I do not think was the case with my ES8228S cleaning base. Still not as good as the Braun module in my opinion.    It carries over my one pet peeve from past Panasonic modules which is no sleep mode. When you come back for lunch, the shaver blinks once every 2 seconds. Blink. Blink. Blink. Gives you the urge to take out the shaver-so what&#x27;s the point of leaving it in until tomorrow? But this is a perhaps a personal quirk and the unit does the job well.    The module is a nice convenience that costs under 15 cents per day and the unit is easily cleaned by rinsing and/or cleaning with liquid soap per the instructions so either way it&#x27;s fast and easy.    Other: Unit has a bright, pleasant blue LED display that shows shave time, battery remaining, I think it indicates when cleaning is needed and it flashes a replace foil symbol after one year. Oddly, the LED goes OFF while you are shaving-but as stated above blinks constantly when done charging. I don&#x27;t know who thinks of this stuff for Panasonic but it&#x27;s odd.    Summary/perspectives: The Panasonic ESLA93K is the best foil shaver I have ever used, without question.    *Should I try it if I am primarily a rotary user? IMO-if you have always preferred the rotary experience you will probably still prefer a rotary to this unit. It is a fantastic shaver but it is a foil experience 100%.    *Should I upgrade if I just bought a recent Panasonic? IMO-if maximum speed, comfort and the sensation of soft closeness is something you are willing to pay for, yes. If ultra Panasonic close is all you need, all the other recent models are great.    *Should I try it if I love my Pulsonic? IMO-yes. To me the ESLA93K is everything the Pulsonic has been to others that it never gave me. It&#x27;s a step above, it is the ultimate foil shaver on the market today.</li>

    <li> I have bought the best available electric shaver, based on Consumer Reports and other tests, for the last 60 years. This has meant buying whatever has been the top Panasonic model over the last 15 years or so, whenever they brought out a new one... so three different models in that time. And I still have all of them, so I can do comparative testing.    The GOOD news. Even the oldest of these three is still fine, has never had anything done to it, including no replacement foil. Wet/dry capability was added two models back. And the shave from each of them has been increasingly smooth with each new model. And with the latest model, you get an auto-cleaning system, probably added to compete with Braun who had it first.     The BAD news. The price has gone up very fast and is now astronomical (except on eBay). But that&#x27;s not the really bad news, which is that the &#x27;trimmer&#x27; has been shrunk so that it&#x27;s now almost useless for trimming sideburns and necks accurately, its main use for most users. It was excellent on both the preceding models, so this is a major backward step and the auto-cleaning system is complex and I never use it or needed it before--just blow the dust out after tapping it on the side of the sink. This is not a trivial error: it&#x27;s like the recalls on the Toyota, a sign that the internal quality control has gone to hell, obviously because they got sloppy from being top dog for so long. No surprise that they lost half a BILLION dollars in the last year, reported today, and are laying off what will amount to a total of several thousand workers. A sad sign that success undermines itself; and guess what country needs to learn that lesson much faster than it is showing signs of doing at the moment.    So I down rate it to four stars, probably should be three.    PS I have six or seven of the little battery operated travel shavers, and the new ones either have no trimmer or a very poor one (as on the current Braun).     <li> If I would have rated this product shortly after receiving and using it, I would have given it 4 stars. The only things keeping it from receiving a 5 star rating were the functionality of the charging/cleaning unit and the retail price. I&#x27;m sorry, but there is absolutely no way that this electric shaver is worth $400 retail. I feel bad for anyone who paid the full price for this product. I picked it up new for around $200 on Amazon. I feel that is a much more reasonable price point for this shaver. The problems with the charging/cleaning unit are 1)it is really not needed, 2)the cleaning cycle is ridiculously long and loud, 3)at the end of the cleaning cycle, the unit emits an incredibly bright flashing blue strobe that continues until you remove the shaver, and 4)there is no separate charging function when placing the shaver in the unit.    After 5 months of daily use, I can disappointedly only rate it at 2 stars due to quality/reliability issues. The charging/cleaning unit is no longer functioning properly. After the last few attempts at using the cleaning cycle, I have found my shaver sitting in a pool of cleaning solution in the morning. The blue led display on the shaver is displaying non-sensical information. For instance, when I last finished charging the shaver, instead of showing 100% charge, the display shows 188% charge. The minutes used/remaining feature displays unintelligible numbers as well. Fortunately, this has not affected the shaving performance one bit, but I wonder about what is going to happen down the road. The shaver is basically controlled by a microprocessor. What if that goes next?    This is my second Panasonic shaver and I continue to be impressed with the pure shaving performance of the shaver, but Panasonic is failing me in the reliability department. It is too bad, because I really think Panasonics perform well. I am not talking about their products failing after years of use. I am talking about their $400 flagship shaver having problems after only 5 months! I do not purchase a shaver of this type for it to end up being disposable. A previously owned Panasonic shaver also had problems with the battery holding a charge. I had it for a little over a year. Panasonic customer service wanted to charge me $40 for a refurbished unit, but gave me a one time credit after I pushed the issue. I have contacted Panasonic in regard to my current problem and told them that I am not interested in a refurbished unit. Hopefully, they will make things right. Fool me once...    UPDATE 5/24/11    After emailing Panasonic through their website and receiving no response, I decided to try calling them. I explained my problems with the shaver to the customer service rep and he provided me with a reference number and contact info for the McAllen Exchange Center. I paid to ship the unit back and within a week of them receiving it, I received a replacement unit at no cost to me. The invoice states that it is a refurbished unit, which is disappointing because I specifically asked them for a brand new unit given the cost of the original unit and the length of time that I owned it. If it is refurbished, I can&#x27;t tell. Everything from the packaging to the shaver and cleaning unit are exactly the same condition as my former brand new unit. While my customer service experience took a turn for the better, only time will tell if this shaver can make the grade in terms of long term reliability.</li>

It took a little longer in the shower because I don&#x27;t have a mirror in there and had to shave by feel, but the results turned out fabulous!  It&#x27;s something I&#x27;ll probably only have time for on the weekends though.  The cleaning station as far as I&#x27;m concerned is far superior to the one that came with my Braun Series 7.  I much prefer the smaller and cheaper dry cartridges to the much larger, messier, and more expensive alcohol based ones that the Braun uses.  I could only get about 6 weeks out of the Braun cartridges even with cleaning the shaver every other day.  The system is not sealed so the alcohol just evaporates whether you use it or not.  The water based system on the Panasonic appears to be much better sealed, and of course you could always add a little more water if you needed to, so I can easily see getting 2 to 3 month&#x27;s out of a cartridge with this setup.  I&#x27;ve always rinsed all the whiskers out of the shaver head first (yes, the Braun&#x27;s head was washable) before putting it in the cleaner base to help keep the load and odor at bay.  This helps the cleaner in the base stay fresher longer and also reduces clogs in the system as well for reduced maintenance.  I&#x27;ll probably only use the wash cycle every few days with the Panasonic because it cleans up so well under the faucet with just using the \\&quot;turbo\\&quot; cleaning method.  The cost of these cartridges through Amazon&#x27;s subscription purchase is only $2.83 each.  I have been paying $4.33 on average for the cartridges for the Braun, and then they only last 6 weeks.  So this will be a nice savings if I can get a few month&#x27;s out of these.  I feel the cleaning system is worthwhile because it keeps my shaver clean, fresh, and dry so much better than if it was just left up to me.  And Panasonic&#x27;s cleaning station allows me to select \\&quot;dry only and charge\\&quot; (where the Braun&#x27;s doesn&#x27;t) so on those day&#x27;s when I choose not to use the cleaning cycle, I can still dry the shaver head in the station which I feel is important to the longevity of the blades.  Plus since there&#x27;s no alcohol in the system, it won&#x27;t erode the finish on the shaver like it did with my Braun.  All the paint flaked off around the base of the head on my Braun due to the alcohol.  I&#x27;m really enjoying my new Panasonic shaving system.  The only gripes I have with it all have to do with the way it&#x27;s programmed to do certain tasks.  Let&#x27;s start with the base.  This is an excellent system and cleans the shaver immaculately.  However, who in their right mind would program it to dry the shaver for 1 1/2 hours!  That&#x27;s right, the fan runs for an hour and a half to dry the head.  That&#x27;s ridiculous!  The cleaning cycle only takes 10 minutes, and that&#x27;s fine.  But it shouldn&#x27;t take more than 20 to 30 minutes max to dry the head with the fan.  Who comes up with these things?  Then there&#x27;s the infamous flashing blue light display that it reverts to after the battery is fully charged.  What would make any one ever think that the customer would be happy with a blue beacon in their bathroom flashing all night long!?!  How absurd is that!  When the shaver is done charging the light should just go out - end of story.  But no, it has to flash and light up the whole room endlessly flashing like a little lighthouse.  Who-ever is in charge of programming these shaver&#x27;s and bases needs to be moved on.  In summary, this is the best electric shaver I&#x27;ve ever used.  And the cleaning/charging station does an outstanding job keeping the shaver in tip top shape.  It is only flawed by a couple of really dumb programming choices.  But I&#x27;ve discovered that you can just tip the shaver to one side in the base to make the flashing blue light go out.  It doesn&#x27;t look quite as elegant as when the shaver is straight but it works.  You can also stop the drying cycle that way too.  Despite these annoying flaws, I still highly recommend this shaver to anyone that wants one of the best shave&#x27;s that can be had from an electric shaver.  Yes, it&#x27;s that good.</li>

Now I can use it no problem no cream. Easier because I have a mirror! I got to cut myself at Adam&#x27;s apple a few times though...  Also, I find that if you are not using for a couple of days, the next shaving won&#x27;t be as good as if you are using it everyday.</li>

    <li> I have been using this shaver for about 1 year now. When I originally saw this shaver on the Men&#x27;s Health awards for best electric razor I was intrigued. Someone else had complained about the upper lip, but the confidence this shaver gives me I have never had a problem getting a perfectly smooth shave beneath the nose.     <li> I&#x27;ve been using Panasonic Wet/Dry shavers for almost 30 years now, so I won&#x27;t go into the discussion on shaving quality. Let&#x27;s just say that shaving performance has gradually improved throughout the years. Instead, I will point out a few features that have changed with recent models:    Improvements:     -Sliding lock for power button. This is a much needed feature for travel. With prior Panasonic shavers it has happened twice that I&#x27;ve gone on a long trip (without bringing the charger) only to find that the shaver accidentally has started in the luggage and run the battery empty.  -The cradle automatically handles charging. You do not need to manually enable charging by pressing a button on the cradle.    Set backs:    -The razor has a very bright blue light that blinks when charging is complete. This is the way it was in previous models (e.g. ES8168) and this is perfectly fine when charging was manually instigated like in previous model. However, the new ES-LA93 cradle automatically handles charging, which means the blue light blinks every day and night. Totally useless and irritating. This blinking is clearly a remnant of previous models and it is an oversight of Panasonic to leave it this way. Needs to be fixed in next version!  -The razor cannot stand on its edge like in the picture. The edge is rounded. You have to lay down the razor. Consequently I always want to store it in the cradle and as a result I am punished with the blinking light. I think this is the first Panasonic shaver I&#x27;ve owned that does not let me store it in upright position.    Missing feature:    -No way to make the cradle default to \\&quot;dry\\&quot; mode. I prefer to clean the razor with hand soap after each shave (as described in the manual, and as I have been doing for 30 years). Then I put it in the cradle to dry. Every time I need to press the button to set the cradle to dry mode. Why can&#x27;t this be automatic? This is how I use the cradle - it should be possible to \\&quot;configure\\&quot; it to do my desiredevery day action automatically. I remove the shaver from the cradle to shave, then I clean it after each use, when I put it in the cradle it should know to start drying automatically.     All in all this new shaver did not meet my high expectations. The ES-8168 was a great shaver and the ES-LA93 only marginally improves things while it adds a couple of new annoyances. Two minor software fixes (disable blinking light and add cradle auto dry) would have made this a 5-star review.    Update: It appears the blinking light annoyance is fixed in the new 5-blade ES-LV81 model.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using the ES-LA93-K for the past 6 weeks. I&#x27;m a long time electric shaver user (20+ years), having used various models in the past - Philips rotary, and several Braun foil models (most recent was the Braun Activator series). This Panasonic is my first wet/dry shaver, and I have to say that it offers the closest and most comfortable shave I&#x27;ve ever experienced from an electric.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are so many reviews for this shaver (mainly positive which led me to purchase mine), not wanting to be repetitive but I&#x27;ll just share some of my experiences &amp; observations:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;Shaver: not as huge as it appears in the images, and not too heavy, fit my hand just right after a short (2-3 day) &#x27;getting used to&#x27; period. The head is on the large side, and took some getting used to / maneuvering for some areas (under nose), but still doable. The nice thing is that the head pivots on 2 axises (side to side, front and back), this is what sets it apart from single axis shavers - it follows the contours of the neck, chin &amp; jawline really well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The foil is very smooth, and glides with hardly any resistance, catching pretty much everything in a pass or two. Even with a couple days worth of stubble (quite a bit in my case), it doesn&#x27;t pinch or snag the hairs like other models I&#x27;ve used. I find that I am taking 2 to 3 minutes less to do the job with this shaver than my Braun predecessor. As for the noise, it&#x27;s a bit more noisy than other shavers I&#x27;ve used - but the motors in this shaver are oscillating much faster than others, so I&#x27;d say it might be the higher pitch that makes it seem louder, it&#x27;s a trade off for an exceptionally close shave. The wet shave / clean feature is a great thing to have. LCD screen is intuitive, showing total shave time, battery level and cleaning indicator.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;The pop-up trimmer is on the smallish side, and due to the placement / head size is hard to maneuver in tight spots. The charging / cleaning base isn&#x27;t overly large, but I am really disappointed in the cleaning time (and noise) compared to my old Braun. The cleaning / drying cycle is 3 hours, and the base uses an annoying fan to dry the shaver. Braun&#x27;s Activator base was silent (and much faster), using an inductive heater to dry. It&#x27;s much faster (and silent) to just wet clean this shaver with a drop of hand soap, and pop the foil off to rinse and let it air dry...no need for the charging base. Another nuisance mentioned by others is the LCD screen flashes bright blue every 2 seconds when it&#x27;s plugged in (or in the base) to indicate full charge. It&#x27;s like an annoying flashing nightlight...a simple LED indicator or unlit LCD would have been perfectly adequate to know when the thing was charged. I would have preferred a rigid travel case for this than the soft pouch they included - to better protect the shaver when traveling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, this offers an exceptionally close &amp; comfortable shave (which is why I bought it); and despite having some design quirks, the pros clearly outweighed the cons in my book.</li>

    <li> Bottom line up front:  This is the best electric razor I&#x27;ve ever owned.  Worth every penny.  Quality product.  FINALLY, a solution to my razor bumps!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ME - I am in the military, which means I have to shave every day.  I hate shaving with an angry, burning passion.  I have been in the military for 18 years and the worst part about the job, day to day, has been having to shave each morning.  Yeah, I dislike shaving THAT much.  I have light skin and coarse facial hair that is very prone to ingrown hairs (aka razor bumps).  I have tried everything to mitigate this condition... yes, EVERYTHING.  A zillion different combinations of blades, techniques, shaving creams/gels, and after shave treatments like Bump Stopper.  I have also tried several other electric razors... other foil and rotary shavers.  I have tried blades and razors and creams reportedly designed specifically for sensitive skin.  I&#x27;ve tried chemical depilatories.  A few years ago, I even underwent several extremely painful laser hair removal treatments to try and get rid of my beard for good... that did NOT go well!  Finally, I&#x27;ve found a combination of products that drastically reduces (although it does not eliminate completely) the number of ingrown hairs I&#x27;m liable to suffer from.  This electric razor from Panasonic is at the center of that combination.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;MY HISTORY WITH THIS LINE OF RAZORS - I am speaking from experience.  Panasonic helped me turn the tide in my battle against razor bumps about 10 years ago.  I&#x27;m estimating this figure because it&#x27;s been so long.  I bought one of the very first models of their Linear foil shaver series... the ES8077, I think.  I only recently replaced it with this newer model, the ESLA93K, because the cleaning/charging station finally gave up the ghost.  Even then, it was probably due to my overzealous cleaning of the unit, that involved running quite a bit of water over (and ultimately inside of) it.  Up until that point, the razor itself, the chargingbase, and the cleaning system worked exactly as well as they did when they were BRAND NEW.  TEN YEARS AGO.  When was the last time you could say that about one of your small appliances, especially one that used some sort of rechargeable battery system?  I wish Panasonic made dustbusters, because I&#x27;ve been through about four of those suckers (no pun intended) in the past decade... they stop holding a charge the second you take them out of the box!  As long as you periodically change the foil, the blades, and the cleaning cartridges, you&#x27;ve got a product that will last you a LONG time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;WHY A PANASONIC LINEAR SERIES RAZOR vs. OTHER BRANDS? - Several reasons I will cover here:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) SPEED.  This is really where these razors shine.  10,000 - 14,000 RPM cuts FAST.  If you&#x27;ve got a coarse beard like mine, a speedy razor allows you to make one or two slow, smooth passes to get all the hairs, keeping you from overworking the area and causing irritation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) BATTERY LIFE.  I think they power these razors with Plutonium.  Two months ago I went two weeks in the field with my ten-year-old razor (and battery of similar age) without charging it and it still shaved with the same power on the very last day as it did when it was new.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) QUALITY.  My razor has survived countless road trips, field exercises, and two year-long deployments to Iraq.  Snap the plastic cover over the foils, drop it in its little pouch, and off you go.  Other than regularly changing the foils, blades, and cleaning cartridges, I haven&#x27;t had to replace a single part.  No dinky plastic pieces sticking out waiting to get snapped off, no chintzy base or poor quality electrical connections or components... it is, quite simply, extremely well built.  That is why, even though the cleaning/charging station died, I&#x27;m keeping the razor itself so that it can permanently live in my shaving kit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) WATERPROOF.  If your face can stand a wet shave (mine can&#x27;t... it cuts too close, then I get bumps), this is a phenomenal razor.  My wife has used mine on her legs sometimes when we are travelling and it leaves them silky smooth every time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5) IT&#x27;LL HACK THROUGH YOUR BEARD LIKE GRANT THROUGH RICHMOND.  I&#x27;ve taken on whiskers at least 1/4 of an inch long (about a week&#x27;s growth for me... I don&#x27;t shave when I&#x27;m on leave if I can avoid it) without doing any sort of pre-trim with clippers.  It takes a little longer, but it&#x27;ll get through it.  Try THAT with a rotary razor!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6) COMPARATIVELY LOW COST VS. BLADES.  You do the math for yourself.  How much do you spend on blades per month?  Multiply that by 120 (number of months I owned my last razor before buying this one).  If it&#x27;s less than the following, then the electric razor is a good deal for you.  I spent $125 for the unit, I changed cleaning cartridges about every four months (a $15 three-pack would last a year), blades every six months ($30 a year?), and the foil every year ($25 or so?).  Yearly upkeep was $70, or $700 for a decade plus $125 for the unit itself, is $825.  Divided by 120 months, is a cost of less than seven bucks a month.  I&#x27;ve also thrown a lot less stuff in the trash over the course of that ten years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;7) WATER-BASED CLEANING SOLUTION.  Other systems use an alcohol-based solution that, over time, will degrade the plastic and rubber components of a razor or charging base.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;8) EASE OF CLEANING.  If you buy one with a cleaning/charging station, then DUH.  Periodic (semi-annual?) cleaning of the cleaning station will help clear out any schmutz that builds up in the water tubes or elsewhere in the base.  Don&#x27;t rinse the whole doggone base under the faucet (see above under \\&quot;reasons why I&#x27;m buying a new razor\\&quot;).  Even without a cleaning/charging station, you just pop off the foil cover and rinse it under the water.  How much easier can it get?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;DIFFERENCES BETWEEN THE ES-LA93K AND MY ORIGINAL PANASONIC LINEAR SHAVER - I haven&#x27;t had it for long, but some things have come to light... some good, some not so much.  See below.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) IT IS FASTER.  Between the higher speed and the extra foil cutter (four heads vs. three), I can shave off a day&#x27;s worth of stubble in less than three minutes if I&#x27;m really in a hurry.  Not really because I can move the head faster, but because it definitely allows me to get a great shave in just one or sometimes two passes.  Fewer passes and less pressure equals less irritation which equals fewer razor bumps.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) MORE COMPLIANT / FLEXIBLE PIVOT.  It took me almost no time to get used to the new configuration, with the head sticking out at an angle from the handle... I like how there seems to be less spring tension on the moveable head, it really allows it to follow the contours of my face closely without requiring much pressure.  It also pivots in two axes, vs. one from my old razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) VIBRATING HEAD.  Okay, I&#x27;ll admit that I thought it would be a marketing gimmick, but it is another great method for reducing the pressure required to get a nice close shave.  Are you picking up on the theme here?  Less pressure &#x3D; less irritation &#x3D; well, you get the picture.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) IT IS A LITTLE LOUDER.  Some folks complained about the noise in their reviews, both for the razor and the charging station when it&#x27;s in its cleaning cycle.  I guess I&#x27;m just used to it.  Still... loud compared to what?  A chainsaw?  No.  A razor blade?  Yep.  Your wife&#x27;s \\&quot;personal massager?\\&quot;  That depends... what kind of batteries does it take?  The point is, sure, it makes noise.  Close the doggone bathroom door for a few minutes and shave your face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5) THE LED DISPLAY IS UNBELIEVABLY BRIGHT.  Okay, no arguments here.  Fortunately, I cannot see into my bathroom from my bed, because if I could, I would have a recurring dream every night that I am a plane, coming in for a landing, and there is a bright blue homing beacon flashing at me through the clouds every few seconds.  Seriously... you could signal aircraft with that display.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6) ONE QUALITY ISSUE (with the cleaning/charging station).  Do an internet search for \\&quot;flashing red status light Panasonic razor\\&quot; and you&#x27;ll come up with a smattering of posts about this.  Considering how I have long touted the quality of this line of Panasonic products, I was a little disappointed to have this manufacturing defect affect my unit.  Fortunately, it was an easily remedied problem.  The error occurs because a microswitch inside the base of the unit gets moisture or water or who-knows-what in it and thinks that you don&#x27;t have the cleaning cartridge inside the base when you actually do.  Since few folks would make the mistake of running a cleaning cycle without the cartridge in there (properly seated), it&#x27;s an easy feature to bypass.  The switch wants to be \\&quot;open\\&quot; (i.e. when there is a fault, the switch closes the circuit path) so all you have to do is undo three screws on the base and snip one of the brown wires leading to the switch itself... now it will think that it&#x27;s \\&quot;open\\&quot; all the time.  Hasn&#x27;t been a problem for me since, but it&#x27;s a shame that I had to take this sort of remedial action as a consumer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;7) THE FOILS ARE ARCHED SLIGHTLY AND THE HEAD IS BIGGER.  I was worried that the bigger head would make the shaver more cumbersome and harder to get into the nooks and crannies of my face, and that the arched foils would reduce the contact patch and cause the shave to take longer.  I was wrong on both counts... it is extremely maneuverable and has no trouble reaching everything quickly and without requiring several passes or excess pressure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;MY SHAVING / FACE MAINTENANCE ROUTINE - For what it&#x27;s worth, here&#x27;s what works best for me.  Your results may vary, but this is the best combination I&#x27;ve found for a close shave that does not irritate my skin and cause razor bumps:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) Shower first thing in the morning, right before the shave.  UseApricot facial scrub (with or without the 2% salicylic acid... I prefer with) [[ASIN:B0000536Y7 St. Ives Blemish &amp; Blackhead Control Apricot Scrub, 6 oz]] to wash your face, scrubbing gently to get a nice deep clean.  Dry face thoroughly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) Prep beard by applying Remington face-saver pre-shave powder stick.  [[ASIN:B00065QS3M Pre-Shave Stick]] I tried Lectric Shave and other pre-shave treatments, but this talc-based powder allows the razor to glide very smoothly.  That means less pressure, which means... yeah, you get it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) Shave against the grain of your face, or across it if the stubble is short enough.  This will help \\&quot;feed\\&quot; the hairs into the foil holes.  The slotted trimmer in the middle of the two main cutting foils will do a good job batting cleanup if you shave in this manner.  I work as rapidly as I can without missing hairs or pressing too hard, because if the razor runs for a long time (unless you are wet shaving) then it will heat up a bit.  This doesn&#x27;t necessarily make it uncomfortable, but it does seem to drag a bit more when it is warmer.  I hit the hardest and most sensitive spots first, then I do my cheeks and sideburns last because they are the easiest and the most resilient, so if the razor has warmed up a bit, it won&#x27;t have as much of a detrimental effect on my shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) Stop halfway through, pop off the foil cover, tap it out, and pop it back on to continue shaving.  ESPECIALLY if you are using talc, you&#x27;ll get stubble and talc residue building up inside the foil cover, so it&#x27;s a good habit to get into in order to keep from overburdening the razor.  Once you have the \\&quot;battle drill\\&quot; down, this takes all of about three seconds to do and get back to shaving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5) Check to make sure you didn&#x27;t miss any stray hairs.  Get really stubborn ones with the pop-up trimmer.  Rinse your face with water to get any remaining talc or loose hairs off.  Pop off the foil cover again and rinse both the razor and the foilcover under the water.  Tap them dry, reassemble, and place in the cleaning/charging station.  If you do not have a cleaning/charging station or you are travelling away from it, I recommend applying Remington \\&quot;Shaver Saver\\&quot; spray [[ASIN:B00006IV41 SP-4 Spray lubricant and cleaner Shaver Shaver - For all Shavers &amp; Groomers]] to the reassembled unit and running it for 5-10 seconds before stowing it.  If you do have a cleaning/charging station, I alternate... one day I will simply set it to \\&quot;dry\\&quot; and the next day I will select \\&quot;clean / dry.\\&quot;  This helps my cleaning cartridges last longer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6) I have a prescription for a combination topical antibiotic and benzoyl peroxide (called Benzamycin) that has really helped keep razor bumps at bay (I rarely, if ever, break out anywhere other than a hair follicle site).  Once my face is dry, I apply the product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;7) After letting the Benzamycin dry for a few minutes, I apply Gillette conditioning after shave gel [[ASIN:B003W3P1TC 2 BOTTLES GILLETTE AFTER SHAVE SENSITIVE SKIN GEL 2.5 OZ.]].  It is not alcohol based so it doesn&#x27;t sting, and it helps moisturize and protect my face (the Benzamycin dries it out somewhat).  My wife also LOVES the way it smells!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;8) Throughout the day, I do my best to keep from touching my face.  Hard to do, but it reduces the chance that I&#x27;ll introduce bacteria into a tiny break in my skin that has been irritated by the shaving process.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;9) In the evening when I get home, I use a face wash (like Neutrogena) [[ASIN:B001EUQBRQ Neutrogena Oil-Free Acne Wash Facial Cleanser, Pink Grapefruit, 6 Ounce]] that has some salicylic acid in it to clean the day off of me.  Then, at night right before bed, I put on another application of Benzamycin and follow it up with the after shave to re-moisturize (and because I&#x27;m about to climb in bed with a beautiful woman who likes the way it smells).  If your face is susceptible to over-drying, you might want to be careful about combining salicylic acid and benzoyl peroxide treatments... my face doesn&#x27;t seem to mind, but your mileage may vary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;10) When razor bumps do pop up, I pull the hairs out with a tweezer.  A dermatologist would probably advise against this, but it seems to let the accompanying pimple heal much quicker with the hair not in there continuing to irritate things.  The biggest challenge for me is to not try and yank out a hair before it&#x27;s long enough to grab.  Otherwise, if you get just a piece of it, it&#x27;ll break off as you tug on it and wind up leaving a jagged-edged hair that is back below your skin.  Recipe for a few more days of disaster right there... better to just leave it alone for one more day and get it when it&#x27;s longer.  Be especially careful not to touch the site where you&#x27;ve removed an ingrown hair... you KNOW the skin is compromised there and you don&#x27;t want to introduce anything that might cause an infection.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;11) On the weekends, or whenever I can, I give my face a break.  It seems to allow it to heal and get ready for the next week&#x27;s battle.  Some might postulate that it&#x27;s better to just shave every single day and let your face get used to it... doesn&#x27;t seem to work that way for me.  If I do wind up having a breakout, continuing to try and shave over an already irritated area just makes it ten times worse.  It&#x27;s like the zits/bumps \\&quot;cross pollinate.\\&quot;  Awesome.  When that happens, the weekend just can&#x27;t get here fast enough for me!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;MAINTENANCE SCHEDULE - Read the manual to see what they recommend.  Now that this razor in particular will tell me when the cleaning cartridge needs to be changed, I will probably just do that upon demand.  Before I was changing the cartridge [[ASIN:B000BF1396 Panasonic WES035P Vortex HydraClean Shaving System Solution Cartridges for Men&#x27;s Shaver (ES8109S, ES8228S, ES8249S, ES-LA93-K, ES-LV81-K) (Pack of 3)]] (and the water in the tank) about every three to four months.  I changed the shaving blades everysix months, and the foil every year [[ASIN:B002N5MHL0 Panasonic WES9025PC Replacement Foil and Blades]].  This kept my unit cutting like new throughout the entire time I owned it, and I will likely keep up a similar schedule with the new razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, hopefully you&#x27;ll find this review helpful.  I know that these razors can be quite an investment, and they aren&#x27;t for everyone.  If you&#x27;re looking for some guidance or reassurance before taking the leap, maybe you&#x27;ve found it here.  No promises, but I can say with absolute certainty that they&#x27;ve been a godsend for me.  If you decide to give one a try, I hope you wind up being as satisfied as I have been.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Best of luck!</li>
    <li> It provides a very close and comfortable shave.  The base is very useful, though the battery life seems quite good.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m a long-time Panasonic user. The shavers are really great for tough beards like mine, and they work in the shower, which is fantastic. I remember reading in a Braun manual once about how a dry shave is always better than a wet shave, and maybe that&#x27;s true for them German beards, but for my beard it most definitely is not (and I&#x27;ve experimented with both).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After three months of daily shaving, I&#x27;d say this is by far the best Panasonic (and closest shaver) I&#x27;ve ever used. It gets all the tough spots and does an all-around fantastic job. I did deduct a star for a few flaws.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The first flaw is that the manual says, \\&quot;it is recommended that you replace the outer foil at least once a year, and the inner blade once at least every two years, to maintain your shaver&#x27;s cutting performance.\\&quot; Ridiculous---unless your beard is made of peach fuzz, there&#x27;s no way the razor&#x27;s blades are going to last the full 24 months. In my 6 years of using Panasonic razors, I&#x27;ve found that after 9 months, the performance is noticeably down from when I first bought it, and that I need to replace both foil and blades. Yes, I have a tough beard.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The second flaw is that the shaver&#x27;s performance depends heavily on how much it&#x27;s charged. Between 70-100% charge it does its best job; between 40-70% it does a good job, but takes longer to get to the same result as 70-100%; and below 40% charge, it&#x27;s basically as good as a Norelco (which is, for my type of beard, not very good). This charge-dependent quality is true not just of this shaver but of all the other Panasonic models I&#x27;ve tried.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The third flaw is the quality of the slider that takes you from flexible grip, to firm grip, to trimmer activation. The slider is extremely easy to trigger accidentally (I&#x27;ve frequently switched from fixed to flexible without intending to do so). Minor gripe here.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The final flaw is with the whole vortex cleaning system. This system suggests you use the same pool of soapy water 30 days in a row (or else spend $$$ on vortex refill pods unnecessarily). I&#x27;m not sure it&#x27;s such a hygenic idea to keep on re-using that water for so long, which is why before using vortex, I make sure my razor is as squeaky clean as possible (using the ultrasound quick clean mode). I would have preferred an alcohol, rather than water-based cleaning system. However, don&#x27;t try putting alcohol inside a vortex system thinking you&#x27;re going to be so smart. I did that on an older unit, and it broke within a few weeks. That having been said, Vortex does get the job done---no mildewy smell ever on this razor (and without some type of cleaning system, be it vortex or something else, you WILL get the mildew, guaranteed, even if you rinse the razor religiously).</li>
    <li> I was satisfied with my Braun Pulsonic 9595 until the trimmer broke so I started the search for a new shaver.  I have a thick beard so I wanted something that would really mow the lawn.  With this new Panasonic I have never had a closer shave, maybe not even with a blade.  Going from the Braun&#x27;s 10,000 cycles per minute to the Panasonic&#x27;s 14,000 vibes is like night and day.  So for me, this was the main selling point.  That being said, there are some areas where the Braun scores.  The shaver head of the Braun is smaller so it is easier to get in those tight corners like under the nose.  The Panny head feels bulky.  The Braun hair trimmer is rounded where as the Panny is flat with sharp corners so shaving the back of the neck is not as comfortable with the Panny if you don&#x27;t hold it exactly flush with the skin. The Braun&#x27;s cleaning solution is alcohol based so it cleans and dries much faster.  The Panny takes about 80 minutes (I think) to dry.  On the other hand, the Panasonic being water based should be more economical over the cost of the Braun&#x27;s Clean &amp; Renew cartridges.  I also like the fact that after I&#x27;m done with the Panny I can just rinse it out under the faucet with some hand soap so I won&#x27;t have to use its self contained cleaning system on a daily basis.  Over time the Braun&#x27;s alcohol based solution started to eat away and peel the paint on the shaver.  The Braun also would leave the whisker clippings all over the sink area where as with the Panasonic the clippings stay under the screen until you pop the screen off to rinse.  One small negative, the Panny has this bright flashing blue charge indicator that is really annoying at night.  It looks like a strobe light from a bad &#x27;70&#x27;s disco movie reflecting off of the bathroom wall.  The simple solution is to unplug the unit at night or turn the shaver around in its cradle after it&#x27;s charged, so not a big deal. If Braun ever came out with a 14,000 vibe unit this would be a much tougher decision.  But for now, Ihave to give the edge to Panasonic.</li>

    <li> I got this for a gift for my husband and he is delighted with his new Panasonic shaver.</li>
    <li> I have sensitive skin, and would often get irritation and burning from shaving, so all these wet shavers that I discovered over a decade ago were real (skin) life savers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve started with the Phillips wet shave (the ones that had a built-in dispenser on the back)...6700 or something, but switched away from them when they adopted the &#x27;open&#x27; system that had all the shavings fall out all over the place, once my 6700 broke.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At that point, I decided to give Panasonic a try, because it had good reviews.  I went with the 8109S (dual-blade predecessor to this one, also foil, wet shaving and cleaning base).  It was great:  much less irritation than the Phillips I had before, and it would clean itself.  I went through two of these (one because the battery died and the price difference to getting a replacement shaver rather than a battery was negligible, the second when my cleaning base died, and I decided to see if this shaver is better).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did not expect the ES-LA93-K (or its sliver brother) to be better, and thought the extra blades are a gimmic, but whatever it is about this shaver, it actually IS better.&lt;br /&gt;The shaves take me 4 minutes (took 7 minutes with the 8109s), which could account for the slightly lower irritation (it was low to beginwith the the Panasonic units anyways).&lt;br /&gt;My chin is definitely less irritated thanks to this shaver really handling it well, whereas with the 8109S, I had to go over it many times to get it cleared (with this one, just once or twice and the chin is cleared).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other observations, for those who may care:&lt;br /&gt;-it&#x27;s made in Japan&lt;br /&gt;-it&#x27;s louder, but the pitch of the buzzing is lower and quite soothing&lt;br /&gt;-battery is Li-Ion, similar to cellphones, where it suffers a lot less &#x27;battery memory&#x27; issues.  This is a big plus for me, as I would always worry with the 8109S that if I charge it every day, it would deteriorate battery life fast, so I would end up doing &#x27;clean, dry&#x27;, but not chargeuntil the battery was down to 30%.  I was a bit worried when I saw that this shaver doesn&#x27;t have that choice (you can only pick clean or dry, but charge is always picked for you as soon as you dock it), until I saw that it&#x27;s an Li-Ion battery.&lt;br /&gt;-cartridges are the same as the 8109S, so I didn&#x27;t have to throw out the spares I had left over&lt;br /&gt;-cleaning is easy.  either dock it and let it clean (the manual gives you 30 days of usage once you start a new cartridge, so no sense in skimping out).  I also use liquid soap (as per the manual) to clean every other time, and the soap I picked is an anti-bacterial, as my sensitive skin means I sometimes get rashes from shaving too (so far, not with this shaver, which I had for a month)&lt;br /&gt;-shaver is heavier than the 8109S, especially at the top, but not too heavy to be comfortable.&lt;br /&gt;-&#x27;shaking out the water&#x27; needs to be done with care on this one-put a finger on the head, and don&#x27;t shake too hard, as the head is mobile, and heavy (in the 8109s, it was just sideways mobile, and stayed put because it was light).&lt;br /&gt;-many users complain about the light, and yes, it is super-bright, and the bedroom looks like an airport at night if the bathroom door is open.  Yes, Panasonic: it&#x27;s nice that the screen is bright, but did it really have to flash every two seconds indefinitely once fully-charged?  I just put a tissue or two over the unit and that&#x27;s enough.  I suggest doing the same to all those whom it bothers&lt;br /&gt;-Shaver works very well with the Nivea Foam that I use (I found this to be the best for sensitive skin, both the white and blue bottles).     <li> The absolute BEST shaver I have used -- much better than my previous Braun.  It gets very close.  Not as close as when I use a double sided safety razor, but about as close as a disposable. The cleaning cycle works great, and the mixture last a long time before needing to be replaced.  Also, it has no smell -- unlike Braun&#x27;s.  Braun&#x27;s cleaner is more of an alcohol based mixture.  Panasonic&#x27;s cleaning cartridges are more of a filter element saturated in a soap.     <li> **I should start out by first prefacing that, before purchasing this, I have been using a Gillette Fusion straight razor for the past 4 years and hadn&#x27;t used an electric shaver since before that time (I had an old Norelco one).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, after being a straight razor user for 4 years, I decided to purchase this electric shaver for a few reasons: (1) Convenience--I could shave anywhere, in the shower, in the bathroom, the car, etc., (2) It was supposed to be really easy to clean (to get a good shave every time), (3) my wife was tired of me &amp;#34;forgetting to shave&amp;#34; in those crucial moments that we are late and need to leave the house right away, (4) it got great reviews, (5) the price was right.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Panasonic ES-LA93-K doesn&#x27;t disappoint. I put a lot of research into which shaver to get and it all seems to come down to personal preferences at the end of the day. The one shining point for me with this was that the general consensus on performance and design was extremely positive from most people that had purchased this Panasonic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;From a non-performance, strictly visual/design standpoint, the shaver is gorgeous, both in and out of the included charger/cleaning base. It is also lightweight and the ergonomics when holding it and using it are really wonderful. You can tell that a lot of effort went into the design of it to get it to feel right in your hand and on your face. My wife also likes the way it looks on the bathroom countertop (which gives me brownie points with her!).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The fit and finish of the base and cleaning system are great too. The shaver slides into the base very easily and rests in it nicely. There is a flashing blue LED that is constantly on when it is in the base that some reviewers have said is bright and annoying. I could give them that for sure. If you are plugging it in and setting it up within eyesight of your bed at night, I could see how that could be an issue. Mine is in my bathroom (away from my bedroom&#x27;s line-of-sight) and so it isn&#x27;t an issue for me at all.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as performance goes--I am, seriously, impressed beyond all expectations. The shaver delivers a very close shave dry with absolutely no irritation of my skin (and I have VERY sensitive skin when shaving normally). That&#x27;s a first for me! It generally takes about 2-3 minutes to get a really solid shave with this and it never feels uncomfortable or awkward to use--it just fits in your hand well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Where the shaver really shines is when it is used &amp;#34;wet&amp;#34; or with a shaving gel (make sure you use on recommended for electric shavers--regular creams and gels will clog up in the cutting heads). It is baby smooth and gets even closer than using it &amp;#34;dry&amp;#34;--again, with zero irritation.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**A side note and recommendation that I have to get the most out of a shave with it, is something that I stumbled upon in some other reviews here (and I am so glad I did!) in regards to shaving cream/lubricant. There were a few reviews that recommended the Billy Jealousy Hydroplane cream with it (also available at Amazon). I wasn&#x27;t even aware of the brand before that and didn&#x27;t even know what it was. It is a specially formulated cream/lotion that is very light and extremely slick (for the blades). I can&#x27;t tell you how awesome the combo of both the shaving lotion and this shaver are--it literally gets as close a shave as I was getting with a straight razor, with no irritation, my skin is actually more moisturized after, and it doesn&#x27;t clog up the blades in the shaver either. The bottle is a bit pricey at $20 or so, but it will probably last about 6 months, and I couldn&#x27;t, at this point, see me shaving without it (even with a straight razor--it&#x27;s that good!).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The cleaning system works well (you need to add some filtered water to the base and &amp;#34;plug-in&amp;#34; the cleaning fluid to it). I have not had any issues so far, and when I use it, the next shave feels just as new and as good as the first. I like that. If you don&#x27;t use the cleaning base (maybe you&#x27;re in the shower, etc.), it opens up and allows you to rinse it very easily too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ultimately, I would say that if you are in the market for either a first jump into an electric shaver, or are looking to replace on that you currently have, I don&#x27;t see a way that you could be disappointed with this. It looks great, feels solid and comfortable, gives a fantastic shave with no irritation to speak of and just performs the way you would hope a shaver would. Panasonic did an excellent job with this and I can&#x27;t recommend it enough.</li>

    <li> I have been shaving with an electric foil razor since around the late 80&#x27;s.  I have always had Braun electric razors until this Panasonic.  During all of those years I&#x27;d say that actual shaving quality has improved little with battery life seeing the most improvement.  Also during that time companies have figured out how to further monetize electric shavers through such things as cleaning systems.  Be it for Braun, Panasonic, etc., it is of dubious value but some make it more affordable than others.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After having Braun for so long I made the switch due to my neck.  As my previous 8-year old Braun 7 Series&#x27; battery started to die, I began looking at alternatives that I thought would have a reasonable chance of finally being a \\&quot;complete\\&quot; razor for me.  By complete I mean a razor I could use without having to do some small clean-up with a manual safety razor as I have always had to do for my neck.  I felt I had given Braun ample opportunity over the years, but while they have always been top notch in reliability and offered a great shave on my face, they have failed continuously to shave my neck to a reasonable degree.  Thus this Panasonic enters the picture.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am not a big fan of cleaning systems which as mentioned before are over-priced and offer dubious value.  I was actually looking at the non self-cleaning version of this razor, when I found I could get this version for $150 here at Amazon.  For less than $20 difference I felt it was a good enough deal especially as it would serve to hold the razor and the cleaning solution itself is vastly cheaper than Braun&#x27;s (although a bit more cumbersome).  Upon receiving this unit I charged it complete in it&#x27;s base overnight before setting out trying it for the first time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will say that I am glad I waited a week before writing this review because my first reactions were not very positive.  However, after spending more time with the razor I began finding better ways to wield it around my face.  My face is well adjusted to foils after all of these years, but I found the angle you use this at to be very important (more so than my old Braun).  Therefore my personal star meter went from an initial two to the current four.  This Panasonic shaved my entire face closer than my old Braun and, most importantly, it does finally allow me to shave my neck to a degree that I don&#x27;t feel I need to clean up with a manual razor.  Clearly a big win.  While it is not perfect and not as close as a blade (at least not on the neck) it is close enough that my manual razor is now in the trash.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Based on the timer function, I find it takes me between 6-8 minutes to shave complete.  Longer than my old Braun, but to be fair, it shaves the neck and overall provides a closer shave.  So, I find this to be a good trade-off.  However, the Panasonic foils do get quite warm (I am not pressing hard either) while the Braun never did.  For this reason I&#x27;d recommend shaving the upper lip area earlier in the process if you don&#x27;t do so already.  I typically did that area last, but found it a little uncomfortable due to the heat.  The neck does take work at multiple angels and frankly there is no part of the face that won&#x27;t require multiple passes.  Despite the size of the head, I certainly don&#x27;t think it is more efficient.  I also don&#x27;t think it glides over the face as easily as did the Braun.  I should mention at this point that I shave dry and will continue to do so.  If I have to buy shaving cream, etc., I have lost what I see is the major advantage of an electric.  That said and you do have the option with the Panasonic while you do not with the Braun.  The best part of this option for me is that I can at least clean it under the water quickly versus the Braun where I had to use a brush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I like the trimmer on this Panasonic more than on my old Braun as I find it to be more precise with my sideburns.  It is a smaller trimmer, but I find it to be a bit more effective.There is a button on the back of the head that allows for free floating head (used for most of the face/neck), locked head (upper lip), and the pop up trimmer.  Very straight forward.  Just one on/off button in front and a superfluous LCD display which shows shave time, battery life, and other status.  I really don&#x27;t think an LCD is required as it is just another thing to go wrong.  External led displays would have been sufficient for the statuses you need.  Additionally, if left charging, the LCD will blink a very bright blue color continuously to let you know it is finished.  Extremely obnoxious.  Why they think that this info is so critical as to require a neon flashing sign is beyond me.  An exit sign in a burning building is okay. Saying that the charge is done...not so much.  I actually place my razor at an angle in the base so that it doesn&#x27;t charge each day and I don&#x27;t have to come in the middle of the night just to be blinded by the thing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The cleaning process is more involved than the Braun which just requires the cartridge.  The Panasonic also requires filling a canister at back with water.  However, given the much lower cost of cleaning solution versus the Braun, and I&#x27;d say this is a fair trade.  The cartridge supposedly lasts as long as the Braun&#x27;s which is daily for 30-days.  Like the Braun I will use it weekly.  The cleaning cycle/drying is extremely long at something over 90 minutes.  I cannot fathom how such a small device would require this kind of time.  That said and you don&#x27;t need to stand there and watch it.  I also don&#x27;t find the noise it makes to be any greater than the Braun&#x27;s system although again it does last substantially longer.  This unit also comes with a carrying case, however, the case is not big enough to house the plug (unlike Braun&#x27;s).  I also understand that, unlike Braun&#x27;s unit, you cannot use this razor while plugged in.  I haven&#x27;t tried this, but frankly it was not a feature I ever needed to use with Braun.  I havenot tested the accuracy of the battery life indicator against reality as I charge it once a week.  The LCD would indicate that it is the best I can get, but again have not confirmed.  I don&#x27;t see this is a big problem.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ergonomics and build quality seem okay, but not up to Braun standards.  What this may mean for longevity is obviously something I will eventually find out.  I would be very surprised if it lasted as long as my Braun&#x27;s have.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It is impossible for me to say whether this performs better than a new Braun would have.  What I can say is that it was much cheaper for me and it does the job.  I think I paid a fair price at $150, but would not agree that this is a $200+ shaver.  Certainly the cleaning system isn&#x27;t Worth $70+ over their non self-cleaning version.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Shaves very close and does an acceptable job on the neck&lt;br /&gt;- Good trimmer for sideburns&lt;br /&gt;- Option for wet and dry&lt;br /&gt;- Much cheaper cleaning solution vs. Braun&lt;br /&gt;- Option to self-clean with soap and water for \\&quot;free\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;- Quick charge if you run out of juice&lt;br /&gt;- At $150 was a fair deal&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- Foil gets quite warm&lt;br /&gt;- Does require work to get that close shave&lt;br /&gt;- Obnoxious flashing blue display&lt;br /&gt;- Extremely long clean/dry cycle&lt;br /&gt;- Travel case does not fit plug&lt;br /&gt;- Cleaning solution doesn&#x27;t smell that great&lt;br /&gt;- Cannot shave while plugged into an outlet&lt;br /&gt;- Too expensive at its current regular $200+ price point&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: I have since found that this razor does not last me a full week on a single charge.  It lasts me about 6-days which equates to roughly 40-minutes of shave time.  The unit will kick off immediately upon reaching zero although since you can turn it on again for a bit, means that the battery isn&#x27;t really dead.  There is only a brief second or two decrease in shave power to alert you to the shutdown.  I can confirm that the shaver will not work while plugged in which is unfortunate.  That said and if you plug in the razor for a few minutes to charge, you should be able to get through a shave afterwords.  In other words it does do a reasonable quick charge to make up for the lack of use while plugged in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2: I thought I would update this review as it has been nearly 1.5 year since my purchase.  I continue to use the blade and foil that came with the unit and I have not noticed any degradation in performance.  Although I was a long time electric foil razor user, I did see my shave times drop after further use of this product to somewhere between 4:45 and 5:10 minutes per daily shave on average.  I would recommend prior to putting the shaver through the clean cycle that you rinse it well.  This won&#x27;t take more than a few seconds and it will prevent the cleaning unit from clogging with tiny hairs.  I also tend to put it through its charge/clean cycle whenever the shaver gets to 20% or less after a shave.  I have found when using it under 20% that it can slow at a certain point so 20% is a good marker to make sure the last shave is a good one.  I still have no troubles in recommending this product as laid out in the review above.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 3: It has now been 2-years and unfortunately this thing no longer works.  There is vibration in the head but the blades no longer move.  Battery is fine and blades/foil were replaced a few months back.  Extremely disappointed in the quality as I certainly expected this thing to last more than 2-years.  Back to Braun for me.</li>

    <li> So here it is... This is a nice razor, in the sense that it looks nice, it is from a good company and works well. All of the positive reviews of this shaver made a believer out of me, a man who has shaved with a blade for almost all of my life. Once you&#x27;re done using it for the day, you&#x27;re done using it for the day, and you don&#x27;t need to use it in the next 3 hours; so just set it in the cleaning cradle and forget about it. The cleaning cartridges are really not that expensive, ($10 for a pack of 3 on Amazon) come on people, stop complaining about that. Now, on to the shave:  This is in fact the fastest shaver head on the market, something ridiculous like 14,000 rpm, this is nice, but it translates to heat... Lots of heat being generated from the head after a couple of minutes of shaving. The shaver does an OK job on the face, nowhere close to a blade, but not bad. The neck and chin are another story. I have a normal chin, no cleft, no crazy jaw-line, just average man-chin. This shaver, along with all others I have tried, does not get close enough on the chin. Inevitably there are 10+ short stubbles left that require cleaning up with a blade. On the neck, even worse. Lots of hairs left behind, especially on sensitive areas which leads to shaving the area over and over and over which leads to...Yes, my friends: razor burn. Not to mention that even after shaving the neck until it is almost raw, I still had to break out my Mach 3 to clean up the left overs.   After lots of after shave lotion, and some salicylic acid to prevent the inevitable ingrown hairs, I&#x27;m writing this review.     <li> After years of appreciating my Braun 8500 series, they went and changed the replacement cutter block and foil, and I just couldn&#x27;t seem to get a decent shave (and yes, Braun apologists... it was a German-made replacement block and foil). So, I thought I&#x27;d treat myself to the [[ASIN:B003YJAZZ4 Braun Series 7- 790cc Pulsonic Shaver System]].
