And, I have to say, I wish I had become a Panasonic convert sooner.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The quality of the shave I got was excellent and consistent. It was comfortable from the very first shave, and only seems to improve. Not a single hair pulled, and not a single cut on my neck. And razor burn? A thing of the past!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also really like how much quieter the cleaning cycle is on this razor, compared to any of the past three Braun razors I&#x27;ve owned. If I forget to clean it after I&#x27;ve shaved in the morning, I can do it before I go to bed without terrifying my family.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So why only four stars?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) Coming from a Braun, the head on this razor is absolutely massive. It would be fine if I didn&#x27;t have a beard and was just arbitrarily shaving, but hitting the line of my beard is really challenging, because the foil is encased in black plastic. So you have to get a feel for where the plastic stops and the foil begins.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) While the Vortex cleaning system seems competent enough, it requires filling a separate tank with water in addition to the Vortex cartridge. You have to pick up the base, unplug it, remove / insert the Vortex cartridge, remove the tank, fill it, replace it, and plug the base back in. By comparison, the Braun Clean &amp; Renew cartridges are pre-mixed, so you push a button, the base pops up, slide the old one out and the new one in. Further, the Braun Clean &amp; Renew bases all have an indicator (or indicators) showing when the solution cartridge needs to be replaced. The Panasonic base doesn&#x27;t do this at all. And lastly, I&#x27;m mildly concerned about what impact my hard tap water will have on the longevity of the razor -- yes, I could pick up some distilled water, but how convenient is that?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) Another base complaint -- the Braun bases look fairly contemporary, and lock the razor in when it&#x27;s being cleaned.  The Panasonic base looks like it&#x27;s from the future, if the future was envisioned in 1981. Yes, it&#x27;s utilitarian, but at this price level, I don&#x27;t think it&#x27;s unreasonable to expect more than \\&quot;functional\\&quot;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) When Braun razors are charged, the LCD (or LED, depending on the model) just shows a charge. This razor continually flashes the blue backlight from the LCD display. Minor? Sure. But again, at this price level, I don&#x27;t expect my razor to look broken when it has a full charge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Individually, I think that list is pretty minor. But taken as a whole, I can&#x27;t say this is a five-star product when there are a number of improvements that could be made that wouldn&#x27;t appreciably change the underlying price of the product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In saying that though, I&#x27;d totally recommend this to anybody looking for a decent electric razor.nd the new one in. Panasonic obviously knows that there is a defect in this unit, yet they have the gall to refuse to send you a new base once it&#x27;s out of warranty. When you spend this much on a shaver, the entire system should last more than 2 years. Now, I don&#x27;t even use the base, as it no longer works. I refuse to pay Panasonic any more money to replace it for a forth time. I simply wash the blades under running water and let them air dry. When the shaver needs charging, I plug it into a wall outlet. The bottom line is that this is an excellent shaver, but because it comes with a defective base. I only give it 2 stars.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been using Braun for a long time - they&#x27;re nice razors, but a bit slow...and with my thick stubble, it typically took about 10-15 minutes to get a shave.     <li> UPDATE: Well, I had decided to not return this shaver in hopes that someday I would like it. I was packing it up and found a leaflet in the box stating \\&quot;stick with it, it&#x27;s worth it.\\&quot; Subtle but effective. So after a couple of months I decided to give this another shot.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You really do have to stick with it-even coming from another Panasonic shaver my face had to adjust. But in the end this unit really does give a good close shave. The vibrating foil does help some, and the battery life is somewhat lacking. But I&#x27;m now six weeks into using this shaver regularly and really like it. For wet shaving in the shower I suggest a small can of shaving gel. A travel-size can will last a while, since you just need a small amount to help the shaver glide over your face. Also, if you intend to use this as a wet shaver consider the version without the cleaning base if the price is less. As a wet shaver the shaver is completely clean after a rinse, and the drying feature of the cleaning base is too time-consuming. So while my original criticisms stand, they don&#x27;t stand in the way of this being a great product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* * *&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have been a long-time Braun shaver user, and until very recently I had a Braun 9595 Pulsonic, now known as the Series 7 that served me well for five years. I&#x27;m also a Panasonic user-a few months ago I also picked up a Panasonic ES-LT71, which is Panasonic&#x27;s entry level 3-blade shaver with a cleaning station. I travel very frequently and sometimes need to pack extremely light, such that the Panasonic is a better choice than the Braun due to weight and size and ease of cleaning in the field. So when my Braun just stopped working, I ordered the Panasonic ES-LA93K after reading so much favorable information about it, and I eagerly awaited the UPS delivery.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The ES-LA93K gives a good shave, but has a few issues. First, the second motor in the head provides the vibrations for the \\&quot;pulsing foil\\&quot; concept, a version of Braun&#x27;s Pulsonicidea. The problem is that while the main motor is 14,000 cpm the foil pulsing motor is much slower and is less effective. It doesn&#x27;t do much aside from draw power. Which is the second issue-battery life. Most shavers now use the same cylindrical Li-Ion battery, but with two motors drawing power this shaver gets much worse battery life. My old Braun or Panasonic LT71 can go almost 2 weeks on a charge, but this one barely lasted a week. With more foils one would expect that this shaver might give a dramatically faster shave, but I found the effect to be less than expected. Next, to accommodate all those foils, the shaver head is comically large. On open areas this does a good job but detail areas such as above the lip or below the sideburns are more difficult. The final issue is the cleaning station. Overall the Braun has a superior cleaning system but it is higher maintenance, where the Panasonic system is less expensive to run. The problem lies with the drying-Braun uses an inductive heater to actually heat the blades after cleaning, and combined with an alcohol cleaning solution the result is a clean and dry shaver in 30 minutes. Panasonic advertises a \\&quot;heated dry\\&quot; but the heat is provided by the friction of running the shaver dry while a small fan blows over the shaver head. This is a missed opportunity, as a small heating element would have done wonders. As it stands now the cycle takes nearly 80 minutes. Overall, the shaver feels good in the hand, is well balanced and well manufactured, but suffers from some design flaws that I hope Panasonic will address in future models. Until then I highly recommend either the ES-LT71 or a Braun Series 7.</li>

    <li> I have owned two of these units - Panasonic ES-LA93-K. I purchased the first one in November 2011 and then its replacement in July 2014. I like the bright blue display but after about six months the display becomes distorted and displays non-sense symbols that no longer indicate battery life, time of use, etc. This is not a deal killer for me, but I assume the problem is the result of moisture getting inside the unit. The first model I owned was used in the shower (as they advertised), and the display went bad in five or six months. The second model I used was only used at the sink and was rinsed quickly after each use - taking care not to dampen the display area, but its display still went bad after six months. So my current Panasonic still works great - but the display now reminds me of the wrist device worn by the alien in the movie Predator.&lt;br /&gt;Another issue is the shave performance. Both shavers gave less of a close shave after about four to six months. I use the vortex cleaning system with my shaver, so I assume my beard wears down the blades and foil over time. After about a year or so, I replace the blades and/or foil. The second shaver showed signs of a drop off much sooner than the first model I owned. This just means I need to shave a little longer to get the same close shave. This might be typical, but I would expect a longer period of like-new performance from a shaver like this.&lt;br /&gt;Still, I have to say there is no shaver out there that has performed where it counts like this one. I also really like the wet/dry aspect of this shaver, but when that is claimed as a feature I expect a more water-tight product.</li>

    <li> I switched from straight razors (Gillette Mach III Turbo) nearly two years ago after hearing a commercial for Panasonic&#x27;s new expensive electric shavers that were supposed to rival a straight shave.  I went out and bought the 4-blade ES-LA63 model which I have been using steadily ever since.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, I recently upgraded to the 5-Blade ES, attracted to the claims that 5 blades will give even a better shave.  At the time of purchase, the LA93K with cleaning system was only $5 more than the LV81 without, so you can guess which one I bought.  I really didn&#x27;t need a cleaning system since I had gotten used to manually cleaning my 4-blade ES-LA63 by running it under the faucet with some soft soap.  For $5 more I am not complaining.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am going to talk to all of you about what it&#x27;s like switching from a straight razor to an electric, just in case you are contemplating doing so.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First thing I need to say is that nothing does as an outstanding shaving job as a straight razor.  While an electric razor can can give you the same perfectly smooth shave that the straight razor provides, it does have flaws.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What these Panasonic electric shavers will provide you with is a shave that is undistinguishable from a straight razor.  In fact, upon completing your shave and running your hand across your face, you would swear that you just shaved with a razor.  The problem?  The neck area is almost impossible to perfectly clean.  This is a common problem with any electric razor.  You will find that there are just small patches on the neck that will never be clean shaven, and thus, touchups may be required from a straight razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Additionally, for those sick of paying the costs of straight razors, I am uncertain that buying a $300+ Electric Razor is really saving you money considering that the blades and foil need replacing every so often and they don&#x27;t come cheap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That being said, there is a real joy to shaving with an electric over a straight razor.  First, you rarely cut yourself.  As much as I love a brand-new straight razor, I hate the inevitable \\&quot;nick\\&quot; that comes with it.  The only time you will cut your face with an electric razor is if you apply too much force, and really, it&#x27;s almost impossible to do.  Secondly, you have the freedom to move the electric razor head across your face in any direction you want, as quickly as you need, without fear of hurting yourself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The best part of using this Panasonic electric razor?  Using it wet.  It actually gives you a much better shave if you wet your face with warm water and apply shaving cream.  If you want the best stuff to use with this razor, I highly recommend Remington KING OF SHAVES gel.  You only need a small dollop of the stuff, but it really does an outstanding job of shaving your face without gunking the razor.  It leaves your face so amazingly smooth you&#x27;ll be touching it with disbelief all day.  And with these gels, you won&#x27;t even need after shave.  Try the Menthol.  Really gives a nice kick to your shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you use the razor dry, I would recommend applying pre-electric shave beforehand.  It really makes a difference.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just don&#x27;t expect shaving miracles the first few weeks you switch from a straight razor to an electric.  You&#x27;ll find a note in the box from Panasonic telling you that great things take time.  They aren&#x27;t kidding.  Your face needs to adapt to the electric razor.  It will take your face at least two weeks (if not more) to adjust the new shaving method and only then will you see optimal results.  I went from a 6-minute shave to one just under 4 minutes.  That is how much my face has adapted to the Panasonic razor over the years.  So, the more you use it, the quicker your shave will be over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After two years of going with an electric, I don&#x27;t miss blades at all.  In fact, I don&#x27;t want to go back to them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Battery goes down about 10% for every shave (mine is averageof 4.5 minutes tops).  Therefor, expect about 10-12 shaves from a full to charge to having to recharge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Is the 5-blade Panasonic better than the 4-blade?  The answer is, slightly.  The 5-blade seems slightly more refined.  It&#x27;s quieter, for one.  It does seem to shave my face faster than the 4-blade, but only by mere seconds.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The charging/cleaning system is nice.  It has a magnet that holds the razor in place while it charges.  The downside is, you need to buy cleaning cartridges once the included one runs out.  If you buy the same razor without the cleaning system it&#x27;s quite easy to clean under a faucet and the application of soft soap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Is this 5-blade razor worth over $300?  Well, if you have the money to spend, then yes.  This truly is the Cadillac of electric razors.  Once you start using it, you won&#x27;t want to shave with anything cheaper.  Just realize that as close a shave as these babies give (and it can be as close as a razor), it will have problems reaching areas of the neck.  This means that you won&#x27;t be able to really give up that straight razor after all.of 4.5 minutes tops).  Therefor, expect about 10-12 shaves from a full to charge to having to recharge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Is the 5-blade Panasonic better than the 4-blade?  The answer is, slightly.
